PRACTICE TEST - SIE EXAM PREP

1. An investor purchases a corporate bond with a face value of $1,000 and a coupon rate of 6%. If the bond is purchased at a premium for $1,050, what is the current yield?
   A) 6.00%
   B) 5.71%
   C) 5.95%
   D) 6.10%

2. Which of the following organizations is primarily responsible for regulating the over-the-counter (OTC) derivatives market?
   A) SEC
   B) FINRA
   C) CFTC
   D) FDIC

3. A shareholder holds 1,000 shares of a company’s stock and is entitled to a 2-for-1 stock split. After the split, what is the new number of shares held and the new price per share if the original price was $50?
   A) 2,000 shares at $50 per share
   B) 2,000 shares at $25 per share
   C) 1,000 shares at $25 per share
   D) 1,500 shares at $33.33 per share

4. What is the primary risk associated with investing in municipal bonds?
   A) Government default risk
   B) Interest rate risk
   C) Liquidity risk
   D) Credit risk

5. Which type of mutual fund is most likely to maintain a stable net asset value (NAV) of $1 per share?
   A) Equity fund
   B) Money market fund
   C) Index fund
   D) Bond fund

6. An investor writes a call option for a stock they already own. What is this strategy called?
   A) Naked call
   B) Covered call
   C) Protective call
   D) Vertical call

7. A market maker offers to sell 500 shares of stock at $25 and simultaneously agrees to buy 500 shares at $24. What is the spread in this scenario?
   A) $1
   B) $24
   C) $25
   D) 500 shares

8. Which of the following is a characteristic of Roth IRAs?
   A) Contributions are tax-deductible.
   B) Withdrawals are taxed as ordinary income.
   C) Qualified withdrawals are tax-free.
   D) Earnings are taxed annually.

9. Which of the following is an example of monetary policy?
   A) Raising income taxes
   B) Increasing government spending
   C) Adjusting the federal funds rate
   D) Imposing tariffs on imports

10. How does diversification reduce investment risk?
   A) By guaranteeing higher returns
   B) By spreading investments across multiple asset classes
   C) By focusing on high-risk securities
   D) By reducing market volatility

11. Which type of investment income is typically taxed at the investor’s ordinary income tax rate?
   A) Qualified dividends
   B) Interest income
   C) Capital gains from long-term holdings
   D) Municipal bond interest

12. What does a stop-loss order do?
   A) Guarantees a sale at the order price
   B) Triggers a market order when a stock reaches a specific price
   C) Limits the amount of loss on an investment
   D) Buys shares at the lowest possible price

13. What should a registered representative do if they suspect a client is using insider information to make trades?
   A) Inform the SEC immediately
   B) Report the activity to their compliance department
   C) Advise the client to stop trading
   D) Ignore the activity

14. Which type of annuity offers a guaranteed minimum return and the potential for higher returns based on performance?
   A) Fixed annuity
   B) Variable annuity
   C) Indexed annuity
   D) Immediate annuity

15. An investor owns 100 shares of a company that declares a 10% stock dividend. Before the dividend, the investor’s shares were trading at $50 each. What happens to the price of the shares after the dividend is issued, assuming no other market influences?
   A) $50 per share
   B) $45.45 per share
   C) $55 per share
   D) $40 per share

16. Which of the following best describes the role of a market maker in the secondary market?
   A) Facilitates IPOs by pricing securities
   B) Maintains liquidity by buying and selling securities
   C) Regulates the market to ensure fairness
   D) Acts as a custodian for investor assets

17. Under SEC Rule 144, how long must an insider hold restricted stock before selling it in the public market?
   A) 30 days
   B) 6 months
   C) 1 year
   D) 2 years

18. Which of the following scenarios demonstrates systematic risk?
   A) A company’s stock price falls after its CEO resigns unexpectedly.
   B) An investor experiences a portfolio loss due to a market-wide recession.
   C) A pharmaceutical company faces losses due to a failed drug trial.
   D) An individual stock’s price drops due to supply chain disruptions.

19. What is the primary difference between common stock and preferred stock?
   A) Preferred stockholders have voting rights; common stockholders do not.
   B) Common stockholders receive dividends before preferred stockholders.
   C) Preferred stock typically offers fixed dividends, while common stock dividends vary.
   D) Preferred stock is issued only by private companies.

20. Which of the following describes the primary risk associated with investing in long-term bonds during a period of rising interest rates?
   A) Credit risk
   B) Inflation risk
   C) Interest rate risk
   D) Liquidity risk

21. An investor purchases a call option with a strike price of $50 for $2. If the stock price rises to $55 before expiration, what is the investor’s net profit?
   A) $3
   B) $5
   C) $2
   D) $1

22. Which of the following fees is typically charged when purchasing mutual fund shares?
   A) Exit fee
   B) Front-end load
   C) Management fee
   D) Expense ratio

23. How are capital gains taxed for securities held for more than one year?
   A) At the ordinary income tax rate
   B) At a reduced tax rate
   C) Tax-deferred until retirement
   D) Not taxed at all

24. What is the penalty for withdrawing funds from a traditional IRA before the age of 59½?
   A) 10% of the withdrawal amount
   B) 20% of the withdrawal amount
   C) No penalty if taxes are paid
   D) Not allowed under any circumstances

25. An investor is considering purchasing shares of a company that is undergoing a stock split. The company's stock is currently priced at $150 per share, and the split ratio is 3-for-1. What will the new share price be after the split, assuming no other market factors?
   A) $50 per share
   B) $100 per share
   C) $75 per share
   D) $150 per share

26. A bond has a coupon rate of 5% and a face value of $1,000. If the investor purchases the bond at a premium for $1,100, what is the yield to maturity likely to be?
   A) Higher than 5%
   B) Exactly 5%
   C) Lower than 5%
   D) Cannot be determined

27. An investor writes (sells) a put option with a strike price of $40 for a premium of $3. If the underlying stock falls to $35 at expiration, what is the investor's net profit or loss?
   A) $3 profit
   B) $5 profit
   C) $2 loss
   D) $3 loss

28. An investor purchases Class A mutual fund shares with a front-end load of 5%. If they invest $10,000, how much of their money is actually invested in the fund?
   A) $10,000
   B) $9,500
   C) $9,000
   D) $9,750

29. Which of the following is a primary responsibility of the Financial Industry Regulatory Authority (FINRA)?
   A) Regulating mutual funds
   B) Overseeing corporate tax policies
   C) Enforcing ethical conduct among broker-dealers
   D) Setting monetary policy for banks

30. If interest rates rise sharply, which of the following bond types would likely experience the largest price decline?
   A) Short-term Treasury bonds
   B) Long-term Treasury bonds
   C) Municipal bonds
   D) Corporate bonds with low credit ratings

31. An individual earns $80,000 per year and contributes $6,000 to a Traditional IRA. What is the primary tax benefit of the contribution?
   A) The $6,000 earns tax-free interest
   B) The $6,000 is deducted from taxable income
   C) Withdrawals are tax-free in retirement
   D) Employer matching is available

32. An Exchange-Traded Fund (ETF) differs from a mutual fund in which significant way?
   A) ETFs are actively managed while mutual funds are passively managed
   B) ETFs can be traded throughout the day, while mutual funds trade only at the end of the day
   C) ETFs always have lower expense ratios than mutual funds
   D) ETFs are subject to front-end loads

33. Under SEC Rule 10b-5, which of the following actions constitutes insider trading?
   A) Trading a stock based on publicly available news reports
   B) Trading a stock after overhearing a company executive discuss non-public earnings data
   C) Trading a stock after its price increases due to market speculation
   D) Trading a stock based on technical analysis

34. An investor sells a stock for $12,000 that they purchased for $8,000 two years ago. What type of capital gain is this and how will it be taxed?
   A) Short-term capital gain taxed at ordinary income rates
   B) Short-term capital gain taxed at a discounted rate
   C) Long-term capital gain taxed at a discounted rate
   D) Long-term capital gain taxed at ordinary income rates

35. A company issues a rights offering that allows existing shareholders to purchase additional shares at a discount. If a shareholder owns 1,000 shares and the company issues a 1:5 rights offering, how many additional shares can the shareholder purchase?
   A) 100 shares
   B) 200 shares
   C) 500 shares
   D) 1,000 shares

36. An investor buys a $10,000 corporate bond with a coupon rate of 4% and a maturity of 10 years. If interest rates rise to 6%, what is the likely impact on the bond's market price?
   A) The bond's price will increase.
   B) The bond's price will decrease.
   C) The bond's price will remain unchanged.
   D) The bond's price will be unaffected by market interest rates.

37. An investor holds a call option with a strike price of $25 and pays a premium of $3. If the underlying stock is trading at $30 at expiration, what is the investor’s net profit?
   A) $2
   B) $3
   C) $5
   D) $10

38. An investor sells shares of stock for $15,000 that they originally purchased for $10,000 five months ago. How will the capital gain be classified for tax purposes?
   A) Short-term capital gain
   B) Long-term capital gain
   C) Exempt from taxation
   D) Ordinary income

39. An investor is considering a mutual fund with a 12b-1 fee of 0.75%. What does this fee represent?
   A) A front-end sales charge
   B) A fee for the fund’s marketing and distribution costs
   C) A fee for early withdrawal
   D) A fee for portfolio management

40. If an individual withdraws money from a Roth IRA before age 59½, under which circumstance would the withdrawal avoid penalties?
   A) The withdrawal is for non-qualified expenses.
   B) The withdrawal is for a first-time home purchase, up to $10,000.
   C) The withdrawal is for luxury expenses.
   D) The withdrawal is for educational purposes.

41. Which of the following best describes the difference between a primary market and a secondary market?
   A) The primary market is where securities are traded between investors.
   B) The secondary market is where securities are initially issued to investors.
   C) The primary market is where securities are initially issued, and the secondary market is where investors trade previously issued securities.
   D) There is no difference between the two markets.

42. Under the Securities Act of 1933, which of the following is true regarding the registration of securities?
   A) All securities are exempt from registration.
   B) Securities issued by the federal government are exempt from registration.
   C) All securities must be registered before being sold to investors.
   D) Only equity securities must be registered.

43. An investor purchases shares in a closed-end fund. Which of the following characteristics is unique to closed-end funds compared to mutual funds?
   A) Shares are continuously issued and redeemed by the fund.
   B) Shares are traded on secondary markets like stocks.
   C) Investors are charged a front-end load when purchasing shares.
   D) The fund is required to liquidate annually.

44. An investor has a margin account with $10,000 in equity and $20,000 in securities purchased on margin. What is the investor’s current margin percentage?
   A) 50%
   B) 33%
   C) 66%
   D) 25%

45. An investor is evaluating two companies in the same industry. Company A has a P/E ratio of 15, while Company B has a P/E ratio of 25. Based on this information, which of the following statements is most accurate?
   A) Company A is considered more expensive relative to its earnings.
   B) Company B is considered to have higher growth potential.
   C) A lower P/E ratio indicates higher risk investment.
   D) The P/E ratio does not provide any meaningful comparison between companies.

46. An investor purchases a zero-coupon bond with a face value of $1,000 for $750. The bond has 5 years to maturity. What is the primary tax implication during the holding period?
   A) The investor owes taxes on the face value of the bond.
   B) The investor owes taxes on the accrued interest annually.
   C) The investor owes taxes only at maturity.
   D) Zero-coupon bonds are tax-exempt.

47. An investor holds a put option with a strike price of $60 and pays a $5 premium. If the current stock price is $55, what is the investor’s net gain or loss upon exercising the option?
   A) $5 gain
   B) $0 gain or loss
   C) $5 loss
   D) $10 gain

48. An investor is considering two mutual funds: Fund A charges a front-end load of 4%, while Fund B charges a back-end load of 3%. Which of the following best explains the difference?
   A) A front-end load is charged when exiting the fund; a back-end load is charged when entering.
   B) A front-end load is charged when entering the fund; a back-end load is charged when exiting.
   C) A front-end load is based on fund performance, while a back-end load is fixed.
   D) Front-end and back-end loads are identical fees charged at different times.

49. An employee contributes $5,000 annually to their 401(k) plan. Their employer offers a 50% match up to 6% of the employee’s salary. If the employee earns $80,000 per year, how much will the employer contribute?
   A) $2,500
   B) $4,000
   C) $2,400
   D) $3,000

50. An investor opens a margin account with $20,000 in cash and borrows $10,000 to purchase securities. If the value of the securities drops to $24,000, what is the investor’s equity in the account?
   A) $24,000
   B) $14,000
   C) $20,000
   D) $10,000

51. Under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, what is the primary role of the SEC?
   A) To approve new securities offerings.
   B) To regulate mutual fund fees.
   C) To oversee trading activity in the secondary market.
   D) To implement monetary policy.

52. A bond with a par value of $1,000 and a coupon rate of 6% is purchased at $950. What is the approximate current yield of the bond?
   A) 6.32%
   B) 6.00%
   C) 5.95%
   D) 6.50%

53. A portfolio manager diversifies investments across multiple industries to minimize losses during a market downturn. Which type of risk is being reduced?
   A) Systematic risk
   B) Unsystematic risk
   C) Market risk
   D) Interest rate risk

54. An investor sells shares of a stock after holding them for 9 months, resulting in a $5,000 profit. How will this profit be taxed?
   A) As long-term capital gains
   B) As short-term capital gains
   C) As dividend income
   D) As ordinary income

55. An investor considers purchasing shares of a company that recently announced a reverse stock split. If the company executes a 1-for-4 reverse stock split and the investor owns 400 shares before the split, how many shares will they own post-split?
   A) 400 shares
   B) 100 shares
   C) 1,600 shares
   D) 40 shares

56. A company issues a callable bond with a coupon rate of 5% and a maturity of 10 years. If interest rates fall significantly after issuance, which of the following is the most likely action the company will take?
   A) Issue additional bonds
   B) Call the bond and refinance at a lower rate
   C) Increase the coupon rate
   D) Extend the maturity period

57. An investor is analyzing an option strategy. They purchase a call option with a strike price of $60 for a premium of $4. If the stock price rises to $70, what is the investor's net profit?
   A) $6 per share
   B) $10 per share
   C) $4 per share
   D) $14 per share

58. An investor sells shares of a stock they held for 14 months, generating a $7,000 profit. How is this gain classified for tax purposes?
   A) Ordinary income
   B) Short-term capital gain
   C) Long-term capital gain
   D) Exempt income

59. An individual contributes $6,500 annually to a Roth IRA. What is the primary tax benefit of this account?
   A) Tax-deductible contributions
   B) Tax-free withdrawals in retirement
   C) Deferred tax on growth
   D) Employer matching contributions

60. An investor considers purchasing shares in a mutual fund that has a high turnover ratio. What is the primary risk associated with high turnover?
   A) Reduced liquidity
   B) Higher transaction costs and taxable gains
   C) Lower dividend payouts
   D) Increased investment duration

61. Which of the following best describes the difference between a limit order and a market order?
   A) A limit order guarantees execution, while a market order does not.
   B) A limit order specifies a maximum price to buy or minimum price to sell, while a market order executes at the best available price.
   C) A limit order can only be placed during trading hours, while a market order can be placed at any time.
   D) A limit order is used for long-term investments, while a market order is for short-term trading.

62. Under Regulation D of the Securities Act of 1933, which of the following investor classifications is required for participation in a private placement?
   A) Retail investor
   B) Accredited investor
   C) Institutional investor
   D) Qualified investor

63. An investor has a margin account with $25,000 in equity and $50,000 in securities purchased on margin. What is the investor's margin ratio?
   A) 25%
   B) 50%
   C) 75%
   D) 100%

64. A company declares a cash dividend of $1 per share. If an investor owns 500 shares, how will this dividend payment affect the investor’s portfolio?
   A) The portfolio value will decrease by $500.
   B) The portfolio value will increase by $500.
   C) The portfolio value remains unchanged, but cash increases by $500.
   D) The portfolio value decreases and cash decreases by $500.

65. An investor is evaluating an Initial Public Offering (IPO) and reviews the company’s prospectus. Which of the following statements accurately describes the purpose of the prospectus?
   A) It provides detailed information about the company’s products and services.
   B) It guarantees the investor a specific return on the IPO shares.
   C) It discloses key financial information and risks associated with the investment.
   D) It ensures the company’s stock will be listed on a major exchange.

66. Which of the following scenarios most accurately depicts liquidity risk?
   A) An investor holds a corporate bond and the issuer defaults on payments.
   B) An investor owns shares in a thinly traded stock and cannot sell them quickly without a substantial price reduction.
   C) An investor experiences a decline in portfolio value due to a market-wide downturn.
   D) An investor’s dividend-paying stock reduces its dividend payout suddenly.

67. Under the Securities Act of 1933, which of the following types of securities is typically exempt from registration?
   A) Corporate bonds
   B) Municipal bonds
   C) Common stock
   D) Exchange-Traded Funds (ETFs)

68. An investor purchases preferred stock that is cumulative. Which of the following benefits does this type of stock offer?
   A) Dividends accumulate and must be paid before dividends on common stock.
   B) Preferred stockholders receive voting rights at annual meetings.
   C) Stock splits occur more frequently for cumulative preferred stock.
   D) Cumulative preferred stock always pays a higher dividend yield than common stock.

69. An investor writes (sells) a call option with a strike price of $70 for a premium of $2. If the stock price rises to $75, what is the maximum potential loss for the investor?
   A) $2
   B) $70
   C) $500
   D) Unlimited

70. A bond with a coupon rate of 6% is trading at a premium. Which of the following is true regarding its yield to maturity (YTM) compared to its current yield?
   A) YTM is higher than the current yield.
   B) YTM is equal to the current yield.
   C) YTM is lower than the current yield.
   D) YTM is not affected by the bond’s price.

71. An investor purchases shares in a mutual fund with a high expense ratio of 1.5%. What impact does this expense ratio have on the investor’s returns?
   A) It increases the overall returns of the mutual fund.
   B) It decreases the investor’s net returns.
   C) It has no impact on the mutual fund returns.
   D) It guarantees higher returns for the investor.

72. An individual is considering contributing to a Roth IRA. Which of the following is a key benefit of this type of account?
   A) Contributions are tax-deductible in the year they are made.
   B) Withdrawals during retirement are tax-free under certain conditions.
   C) There are no income limits for contributing to a Roth IRA.
   D) Required minimum distributions (RMDs) begin at age 72.

73. An investor opens a margin account and deposits $10,000. The broker sets the initial margin requirement at 50%. What is the maximum amount of securities the investor can purchase?
   A) $10,000
   B) $20,000
   C) $15,000
   D) $5,000

74. An investor receives interest income from municipal bonds. How is this income typically taxed?
   A) Subject to federal and state taxes.
   B) Exempt from federal taxes but may be subject to state taxes.
   C) Exempt from both federal and state taxes.
   D) Subject to capital gains taxes.

75. An investor owns 200 shares of a company that announces a 3-for-1 stock split. After the split, what will be the total number of shares the investor owns, and how will the share price change?
   A) 600 shares; the share price will increase by three times.
   B) 600 shares; the share price will be one-third of the original price.
   C) 200 shares; the share price will remain the same.
   D) 600 shares; the share price will remain unchanged.

76. A bond has a coupon rate of 4% and is trading at a discount. Which of the following statements is most accurate regarding its yield to maturity (YTM)?
   A) The YTM will be lower than the coupon rate.
   B) The YTM will be equal to the coupon rate.
   C) The YTM will be higher than the coupon rate.
   D) The YTM will not be impacted by the bond's trading price.

77. An investor writes (sells) a covered call on a stock they own with a strike price of $50 and receives a $2 premium. If the stock price rises to $55 at expiration, what is the investor's total gain?
   A) $2 per share.
   B) $7 per share.
   C) $5 per share.
   D) $3 per share.

78. An investor purchases a mutual fund with a net asset value (NAV) of $25 per share and a sales charge of 4%. What is the public offering price (POP) of the mutual fund?
   A) $24.04
   B) $25.00
   C) $26.04
   D) $27.00

79. Under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, which of the following entities is responsible for maintaining fair and orderly markets?
   A) The SEC
   B) FINRA
   C) Exchanges like NYSE and NASDAQ
   D) The Federal Reserve

80. An investor holds a municipal bond in their portfolio. What is the primary tax advantage of this type of bond?
   A) Interest is exempt from federal taxes.
   B) Interest is exempt from state taxes.
   C) Capital gains are tax-free.
   D) All income is tax-deferred.

81. An individual takes a $10,000 distribution from their Traditional IRA at age 55. What are the tax implications of this withdrawal?
   A) The entire amount is tax-free.
   B) The entire amount is subject to ordinary income tax and a 10% penalty.
   C) The entire amount is subject to a 10% penalty only.
   D) The entire amount is subject to capital gains tax.

82. Which of the following best describes a dark pool?
   A) A public exchange for trading securities.
   B) A private marketplace for institutional trading with limited transparency.
   C) A fund that invests in high-risk securities.
   D) A type of algorithmic trading strategy.

83. An investor wants to hedge the risk of a declining stock price. Which of the following strategies would be most effective?
   A) Writing a covered call.
   B) Buying a put option.
   C) Selling the stock short.
   D) Buying a call option.

84. An investor is considering purchasing shares of a no-load mutual fund. What does 'no-load' mean?
   A) The fund has no transaction fees.
   B) The fund has no sales charges.
   C) The fund has no management fees.
   D) The fund has no expense ratio.

85. An investor is considering an exchange-traded fund (ETF) that tracks the S&P 500 index. What is one significant benefit of investing in an ETF compared to a mutual fund?
   A) ETFs generally have lower expense ratios.
   B) ETFs can only be traded at the end of the trading day.
   C) ETFs are guaranteed to outperform mutual funds.
   D) ETFs do not pay dividends.

86. An investor writes (sells) a put option with a strike price of $40 and receives a premium of $2. If the stock price drops to $35, what is the investor's maximum potential loss?
   A) $3 per share
   B) $5 per share
   C) $40 per share
   D) $38 per share

87. A company announces a forward stock split of 2-for-1. An investor currently owns 300 shares of the company. After the split, what will the investor’s new share count be?
   A) 150 shares
   B) 300 shares
   C) 600 shares
   D) 900 shares

88. An investor considers purchasing a high-yield bond. Which of the following risks is most associated with high-yield bonds?
   A) Liquidity risk
   B) Credit risk
   C) Interest rate risk
   D) Currency risk

89. Under the Securities Act of 1933, which of the following is required for an issuer to legally offer securities to the public?
   A) A prospectus and registration statement
   B) Approval from FINRA
   C) A market order
   D) An underwriter guarantee

90. An investor opens a margin account and purchases $30,000 of securities by depositing $15,000 in cash. What is the investor's initial margin requirement based on Regulation T?
   A) $7,500
   B) $15,000
   C) $20,000
   D) $30,000

91. An individual contributes to a Traditional IRA. Which of the following is a key tax advantage of this type of account?
   A) Distributions are tax-free.
   B) Contributions are tax-deductible.
   C) Withdrawals before age 59½ incur no penalties.
   D) Capital gains within the account are taxed annually.

92. Which of the following best describes the role of the NYSE specialist?
   A) To execute trades at the best possible price
   B) To maintain an orderly market by buying and selling shares
   C) To represent retail investors
   D) To regulate trading activity

93. An investor reviews a mutual fund with a front-end load of 5%. How does this fee impact the investor?
   A) It reduces the net asset value (NAV).
   B) It is deducted from the total investment amount.
   C) It applies to the annual returns.
   D) It is charged during redemption.

94. An investor holds a long straddle position, buying both a put and a call option on the same stock with the same strike price of $50. What type of market movement does this strategy aim to benefit from?
   A) Minimal price movement
   B) Significant price movement in either direction
   C) Stock price decline only
   D) Stock price increase only

95. An investor purchases a corporate bond with a par value of $1,000 and a coupon rate of 5%. If the bond is purchased at a price of $1,050, what is the yield to maturity likely to be?
   A) Above 5%
   B) Exactly 5%
   C) Below 5%
   D) Cannot be determined

96. An investor reviews a company's balance sheet and notices an increase in retained earnings. What does this typically indicate?
   A) The company has issued new shares of stock.
   B) The company has net profits and has reinvested them.
   C) The company has taken on additional debt.
   D) The company has paid out large dividends.

97. An investor sells municipal bonds and experiences a capital gain of $3,000. How is this gain taxed?
   A) Capital gains are tax-exempt for municipal bonds.
   B) Capital gains are taxed at the investor's income tax rate.
   C) Capital gains are taxed at the long-term capital gains rate.
   D) Capital gains are taxed at the short-term capital gains rate.

98. An investor is considering a real estate investment trust (REIT). What is a key characteristic of this type of investment?
   A) REITs are exempt from all taxes.
   B) REITs must distribute at least 90% of taxable income to shareholders.
   C) REITs are only available to institutional investors.
   D) REITs cannot be traded on public exchanges.

99. An investor writes (sells) a put option with a strike price of $50 and collects a $3 premium. If the stock's price falls to $45, what is the investor's net loss or gain?
   A) $2 loss
   B) $3 gain
   C) $2 gain
   D) $5 loss

100. An investor places a stop-limit order to sell shares at a stop price of $50 and a limit price of $48. What will happen if the stock price drops to $49 and stays there?
   A) The shares will sell at $48.
   B) The shares will remain unsold.
   C) The shares will sell at $49.
   D) The order will be canceled.

101. An investor is constructing a portfolio and decides to allocate 60% to stocks, 30% to bonds, and 10% to cash. Which concept does this strategy exemplify?
   A) Diversification
   B) Asset allocation
   C) Sector rotation
   D) Market timing

102. Under Rule 144 of the Securities Act of 1933, what is the holding period requirement for restricted securities before they can be sold?
   A) 1 month
   B) 6 months
   C) 12 months
   D) 18 months

103. An investor is concerned about currency risk in international investments. Which of the following strategies can help mitigate this risk?
   A) Investing in U.S. Treasury bonds

   B) Guaranteed returns
   C) Tax-free income

1924. An investor purchases foreign bonds. What type of risk is most likely to affect this investment?
   A) Inflation risk
   B) Currency risk
   C) Liquidity risk
   D) Credit risk

1925. An investor places a market order to buy 500 shares. What is the primary characteristic of a market order?
   A) It executes immediately at the best available price
   B) It sets a specific price for execution
   C) It guarantees execution at the investor’s desired price
   D) It is executed only during market close

1926. Under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, what is the primary purpose of the SEC?
   A) To provide investment advice to investors
   B) To ensure fair and efficient securities markets
   C) To set monetary policy for the economy
   D) To regulate mutual fund fees



--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Current yield is calculated as Annual Coupon Payment / Price Paid for the Bond. In this case, the annual coupon payment is $60 (6% of $1,000), and the bond price is $1,050. The current yield is therefore $60 / $1,050 = 5.71%.

2. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The Commodity Futures Trading Commission (CFTC) is the federal agency that regulates the trading of derivatives, including the over-the-counter market.

3. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A 2-for-1 stock split doubles the number of shares held while halving the price per share. The new number of shares is 2,000, and the new price per share is $25.

4. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The primary risk associated with municipal bonds is interest rate risk, as the value of fixed-income securities typically decreases when interest rates rise.

5. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Money market funds generally aim to maintain a stable NAV of $1 per share by investing in short-term, low-risk securities.

6. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A covered call strategy involves selling (writing) a call option for a stock the investor already owns, which helps generate income from premiums while limiting upside potential.

7. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The spread is the difference between the ask price ($25) and the bid price ($24), which is $1.

8. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Qualified withdrawals from a Roth IRA are tax-free because contributions are made with after-tax dollars.

9. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Monetary policy involves actions taken by a central bank, such as adjusting interest rates, to influence the economy.

10. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Diversification reduces risk by spreading investments across various asset classes, sectors, or geographic regions, thereby minimizing the impact of poor performance in any single investment.

11. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Interest income from most bonds and savings accounts is taxed at the investor’s ordinary income tax rate.

12. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A stop-loss order becomes a market order once the stock reaches a specified price, helping investors manage downside risk.

13. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Registered representatives should report suspected insider trading to their firm's compliance department for further investigation.

14. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: An indexed annuity provides a guaranteed minimum return and a potential for higher returns linked to the performance of an underlying index, such as the S&P 500.

15. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: When a company declares a stock dividend, the total number of shares increases, but the total market value remains the same. In this case, the 10% stock dividend increases the investor’s shares to 110. To find the new price per share, divide the original total value ($50 x 100 = $5000) by the new number of shares (110). The new price per share is approximately $45.45.

16. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A market maker exists in the secondary market to maintain liquidity by providing buy and sell quotes for securities. They ensure there is always a market for securities by trading from their own account.

17. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Rule 144 requires a minimum holding period of 6 months for restricted stock held by insiders before it can be sold in the public market, provided that the issuer is subject to reporting requirements under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934.

18. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Systematic risk refers to risks that affect the entire market or economy. A market-wide recession impacts all investors and cannot be avoided through diversification, making it an example of systematic risk.

19. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Preferred stockholders typically receive fixed dividends and have a higher claim on assets in case of liquidation compared to common stockholders. Common stock dividends depend on company performance and are not guaranteed.

20. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Interest rate risk is the risk that rising interest rates will lead to falling bond prices, especially for long-term bonds. This occurs because new bonds will offer higher yields, making existing bonds with lower yields less attractive.

21. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The call option allows the investor to buy the stock at $50. Selling the stock at $55 yields a $5 profit, but the investor paid $2 for the option. The net profit is $5 - $2 = $3.

22. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A front-end load is a sales charge applied when mutual fund shares are purchased. Management fees and expense ratios are ongoing costs, while exit fees may apply when shares are sold.

23. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Capital gains on securities held for more than one year are taxed at the long-term capital gains rate, which is generally lower than the ordinary income tax rate.

24. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Withdrawing funds from a traditional IRA before age 59½ incurs a 10% penalty, in addition to ordinary income taxes, unless an exception applies.

25. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: In a 3-for-1 stock split, the number of shares triples, and the price per share is divided by 3. Thus, $150 ÷ 3 = $50 per share.

26. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: When a bond is purchased at a premium, the yield to maturity will be lower than the coupon rate because the investor is paying more than the face value.

27. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The investor receives a $3 premium but must buy the stock at $40 when it's worth $35, incurring a $5 loss. Net profit/loss = $3 - $5 = $2 loss.

28. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A front-end load reduces the initial investment by the load percentage. $10,000 × (1 - 0.05) = $9,500.

29. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: FINRA is responsible for ensuring ethical practices among broker-dealers and protecting investors.

30. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Long-term bonds are more sensitive to interest rate changes due to their longer duration.

31. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Contributions to a Traditional IRA reduce taxable income in the year of the contribution.

32. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: ETFs trade on exchanges like stocks, allowing for intraday trading, while mutual funds settle at the end of the day.

33. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Trading on material, non-public information is prohibited under SEC Rule 10b-5.

34. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Because the stock was held for over one year, the profit qualifies as a long-term capital gain and is taxed at a discounted rate.

35. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A 1:5 rights offering means the shareholder can purchase 1 additional share for every 5 shares owned. Since the shareholder owns 1,000 shares, they can purchase 1,000 ÷ 5 = 200 additional shares.

36. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Bond prices and interest rates are inversely related. If interest rates rise, the bond's price will decrease because its fixed coupon payments become less attractive compared to newly issued bonds with higher rates.

37. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: At expiration, the stock is trading at $30, which is $5 above the strike price of $25. The investor's profit is $5 (intrinsic value) minus the $3 premium paid, resulting in a net profit of $2.

38. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Capital gains are classified as short-term if the asset is held for one year or less. Since the stock was held for only five months, the gain will be classified as a short-term capital gain.

39. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A 12b-1 fee is charged by some mutual funds to cover marketing, advertising, and distribution expenses. It is expressed as a percentage of the fund's assets.

40. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Roth IRA withdrawals avoid penalties if they meet certain exceptions, such as a first-time home purchase (up to $10,000), qualified educational expenses, or substantial medical expenses.

41. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The primary market is where securities are initially issued to investors, while the secondary market is where those securities are traded among investors after issuance.

42. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Securities issued by the federal government are exempt from registration under the Securities Act of 1933, along with other exempted securities such as municipal bonds and certain private placements.

43. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Closed-end funds have a fixed number of shares that are traded on secondary markets, similar to stocks. Mutual funds, on the other hand, continuously issue and redeem shares directly with investors.

44. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The margin percentage is calculated as equity divided by the total market value of the securities. In this case, $10,000 ÷ $20,000 = 50%.

45. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A higher P/E ratio typically indicates that investors expect higher growth potential or future earnings from the company.

46. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Even though no interest is paid until maturity, the IRS requires investors to pay taxes on accrued interest each year as if it were received.

47. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The investor can sell the stock at $60, resulting in a $5 profit after deducting the $5 premium paid.

48. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A front-end load is charged upon initial purchase of fund shares, while a back-end load is charged when selling shares of the fund.

49. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The employer matches 50% of the employee's contributions up to 6% of their salary ($80,000 x 6% = $4,800). Therefore, the employer contributes $2,400.

50. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Equity is calculated as the value of the securities minus the loan amount ($24,000 - $10,000 = $14,000).

51. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The SEC oversees the trading activity in the secondary market to ensure fairness and transparency.

52. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Current yield is calculated as annual interest ($60) divided by the purchase price ($950), which equals approximately 6.32%.

53. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Unsystematic risk is reduced through diversification, while systematic risk cannot be eliminated through diversification.

54. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Profits from securities held for less than one year are taxed as short-term capital gains, which are taxed at the investor’s ordinary income tax rate.

55. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: In a 1-for-4 reverse stock split, the number of shares owned is divided by 4. Therefore, owning 400 shares pre-split results in 100 shares post-split.

56. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Callable bonds allow issuers to redeem bonds early, usually to refinance at lower rates if interest rates fall.

57. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The profit is calculated as the increase in stock price above the strike price ($70 - $60 = $10) minus the premium paid ($10 - $4 = $6).

58. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: A gain on securities held for more than one year is classified as a long-term capital gain, which typically has favorable tax treatment.

59. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Contributions to a Roth IRA are made with after-tax dollars, and qualified withdrawals in retirement are tax-free.

60. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: High turnover in a mutual fund leads to increased trading costs and potential taxable gains for the investor.

61. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Limit orders specify a price threshold for buying or selling, while market orders prioritize speed and execute at the best available price.

62. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Regulation D allows private placements to be sold to accredited investors, who meet specific income or net worth criteria.

63. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Margin ratio is calculated as equity divided by the total value of securities ($25,000 / $50,000 = 50%).

64. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Dividends are paid in cash, increasing the investor's cash balance without changing the overall portfolio value.

65. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The prospectus is a legal document that outlines key financial information and potential risks to help investors make informed decisions about the IPO.

66. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Liquidity risk occurs when an investor cannot sell an asset quickly at its fair market value due to low trading volume or demand.

67. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Municipal bonds are often exempt from registration under the Securities Act of 1933 because they are issued by state and local governments.

68. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Cumulative preferred stock requires that any unpaid dividends be paid to preferred stockholders before dividends are paid to common shareholders.

69. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: When an investor writes a call option, their potential loss is unlimited because the stock price can theoretically rise indefinitely.

70. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: For a bond trading at a premium, the yield to maturity is lower than the current yield because the investor is paying above the bond’s face value.

71. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A high expense ratio reduces the net returns to the investor because it represents the annual fee charged by the mutual fund to cover its operating costs.

72. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A major advantage of Roth IRAs is that qualified withdrawals during retirement are tax-free.

73. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: With a 50% margin requirement, the investor can borrow an additional $10,000, allowing them to purchase up to $20,000 worth of securities.

74. Correct Answer: B
